tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   320→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   321→\n   322→\t// Output results live in the module that declares them, which is one of\n   323→\t// the child module instances of our current module path.\n   324→\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath.Module().Child(addr.Name)\n   325→\tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n   326→\n   327→\tparentCfg := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendentForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n   328→\tcallConfig, ok := parentCfg.Module.ModuleCalls[addr.Name]\n   329→\tif !ok {\n   330→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   331→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   332→\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared module`,\n   333→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The configuration contains no %s.`, moduleAddr),\n   334→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   335→\t\t})\n   336→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   337→\t}\n   338→\n   339→\t// We'll consult the configuration to see what output names we are\n   340→\t// expecting, so we can ensure the resulting object is of the expected\n   341→\t// type even if our data is incomplete for some reason.\n   342→\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.Descendent(moduleAddr)\n   343→\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n   344→\t\t// should never happen, since we have a valid module call above, this\n   345→\t\t// should be caught during static validation.\n   346→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"output value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n   347→\t}\n   348→\toutputConfigs := moduleConfig.Module.Outputs\n   349→\n   350→\t// We don't do instance expansion during validation, and so we need to\n   351→\t// return an unknown value. Technically we should always return\n   352→\t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n   353→\t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n   354→\t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n   355→\t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n   356→\t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n   357→\t// validation.\n   358→\t//\n   359→\t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n   360→\t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n   361→\t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n   362→\t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n   363→\tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n   364→\t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n   365→\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n   366→\t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n   367→\t\t}\n   368→\t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n   369→\n   370→\t\tswitch {\n   371→\t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n   372→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n   373→\t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n   374→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n   375→\t\tdefault:\n   376→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n   377→\t\t}\n   378→\t}\n   379→\n   380→\t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n   381→\t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n   382→\t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n   383→\t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n   384→\tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n   385→\tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n   386→\tif !known {\n   387→\t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n   388→\t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n   389→\t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n   390→\t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n   391→\t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n   392→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   393→\t}\n   394→\n   395→\tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   396→\t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n   397→\t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n   398→\t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   399→\n   400→\t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n   401→\t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n   402→\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n   403→\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n   404→\t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n   405→\n   406→\t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n   407→\t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n   408→\t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n   409→\t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n   410→\t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n   411→\t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n   412→\t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n   413→\t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n   414→\t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n   415→\t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n   416→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   417→\t\t\t}\n   418→\t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n   419→\t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n   420→\t\t}\n   421→\n   422→\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n   423→\t}\n   424→\n   425→\tswitch instKeyType {\n   426→\n   427→\tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n   428→\t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n   429→\t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n   430→\t\t// implementation.\n   431→\t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n   432→\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n   433→\t\t}\n   434→\t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n   435→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   436→\t\treturn ret, diags\n   437→\n   438→\tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n   439→\t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n   440→\t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n   441→\t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n   442→\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n   443→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n   444→\t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n   445→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   446→\t\t}\n   447→\t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n   448→\n   449→\tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n   450→\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n   451→\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n   452→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n   453→\t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n   454→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   455→\t\t}\n   456→\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n   457→\n   458→\tdefault:\n   459→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   460→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   461→\t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n   462→\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n   463→\t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n   464→\t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n   465→\t\t\t),\n   466→\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   467→\t\t})\n   468→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   469→\t}\n   470→}\n   471→\n   472→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetPathAttr(addr addrs.PathAttr, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   473→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   474→\tswitch addr.Name {\n   475→\n   476→\tcase \"cwd\":\n   477→\t\tvar err error\n   478→\t\tvar wd string\n   479→\t\tif d.Evaluator.Meta != nil {\n   480→\t\t\t// Meta is always non-nil in the normal case, but some test cases\n   481→\t\t\t// are not so realistic.\n   482→\t\t\twd = d.Evaluator.Meta.OriginalWorkingDir\n   483→\t\t}\n   484→\t\tif wd == \"\" {\n   485→\t\t\twd, err = os.Getwd()\n   486→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   487→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   488→\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   489→\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Failed to get working directory`,\n   490→\t\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The value for path.cwd cannot be determined due to a system error: %s`, err),\n   491→\t\t\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   492→\t\t\t\t})\n   493→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   494→\t\t\t}\n   495→\t\t}\n   496→\t\t// The current working directory should always be absolute, whether we\n   497→\t\t// just looked it up or whether we were relying on ContextMeta's\n   498→\t\t// (possibly non-normalized) path.\n   499→\t\twd, err = filepath.Abs(wd)\n   500→\t\tif err != nil {\n   501→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   502→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   503→\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Failed to get working directory`,\n   504→\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The value for path.cwd cannot be determined due to a system error: %s`, err),\n   505→\t\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   506→\t\t\t})\n   507→\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   508→\t\t}\n   509→\n   510→\t\treturn cty.StringVal(filepath.ToSlash(wd)), diags\n   511→\n   512→\tcase \"module\":\n   513→\t\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendentForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n   514→\t\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n   515→\t\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n   516→\t\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n   517→\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module.path read from module %s, which has no configuration\", d.ModulePath))\n   518→\t\t}\n   519→\t\tsourceDir := moduleConfig.Module.SourceDir\n   520→\t\treturn cty.StringVal(filepath.ToSlash(sourceDir)), diags\n   521→\n   522→\tcase \"root\":\n   523→\t\tsourceDir := d.Evaluator.Config.Module.SourceDir\n   524→\t\treturn cty.StringVal(filepath.ToSlash(sourceDir)), diags\n   525→\n   526→\tdefault:\n   527→\t\tsuggestion := didyoumean.NameSuggestion(addr.Name, []string{\"cwd\", \"module\", \"root\"})\n   528→\t\tif suggestion != \"\" {\n   529→\t\t\tsuggestion = fmt.Sprintf(\" Did you mean %q?\", suggestion)\n   530→\t\t}\n   531→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   532→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   533→\t\t\tSummary:  `Invalid \"path\" attribute`,\n   534→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The \"path\" object does not have an attribute named %q.%s`, addr.Name, suggestion),\n   535→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   536→\t\t})\n   537→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   538→\t}\n   539→}\n   540→\n   541→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   542→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   543→\t// First we'll consult the configuration to see if an resource of this\n   544→\t// name is declared at all.\n   545→\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath\n   546→\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendentForInstance(moduleAddr)\n   547→\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n   548→\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n   549→\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n   550→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"resource value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n   551→\t}\n   552→\n   553→\tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.ResourceByAddr(addr)\n   554→\tif config == nil {\n   555→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   556→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   557→\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared resource`,\n   558→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A resource %q %q has not been declared in %s`, addr.Type, addr.Name, moduleDisplayAddr(moduleAddr)),\n   559→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   560→\t\t})\n   561→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   562→\t}\n   563→\n   564→\t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n   565→\t// state available in all cases.\n   566→\t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n   567→\t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n   568→\tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n   569→\tif schema == nil {\n   570→\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here should've\n   571→\t\t// taken care of it, but we'll show a reasonable error message anyway.\n   572→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   573→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   574→\t\t\tSummary:  `Missing resource type schema`,\n   575→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"No schema is available for %s in %s. This is a bug in Terraform and should be reported.\", addr, config.Provider),\n   576→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   577→\t\t})\n   578→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   579→\t}\n   580→\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n   581→\n   582→\trs := d.Evaluator.State.Resource(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n   583→\n   584→\tif rs == nil {\n   585→\t\tswitch d.Operation {\n   586→\t\tcase walkPlan, walkApply:\n   587→\t\t\t// During plan and apply as we evaluate each removed instance they\n   588→\t\t\t// are removed from the working state. Since we know there are no\n   589→\t\t\t// instances, return an empty container of the expected type.\n   590→\t\t\tswitch {\n   591→\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   592→\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyTupleVal, diags\n   593→\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   594→\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyObjectVal, diags\n   595→\t\t\tdefault:\n   596→\t\t\t\t// While we can reference an expanded resource with 0\n   597→\t\t\t\t// instances, we cannot reference instances that do not exist.\n   598→\t\t\t\t// Due to the fact that we may have direct references to\n   599→\t\t\t\t// instances that may end up in a root output during destroy\n   600→\t\t\t\t// (since a planned destroy cannot yet remove root outputs), we\n   601→\t\t\t\t// need to return a dynamic value here to allow evaluation to\n   602→\t\t\t\t// continue.\n   603→\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] unknown instance %q referenced during %s\", addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath), d.Operation)\n   604→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   605→\t\t\t}\n   606→\n   607→\t\tcase walkImport:\n   608→\t\t\t// Import does not yet plan resource changes, so new resources from\n   609→\t\t\t// config are not going to be found here. Once walkImport fully\n   610→\t\t\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\n   611→\t\t\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\n   612→\t\t\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\n   613→\t\t\t// value. This of course will not help if statically known\n   614→\t\t\t// attributes are expected to be known elsewhere, but reduces the\n   615→\t\t\t// number of problematic configs for now.\n   616→\t\t\t// Unlike in plan and apply above we can't be sure the count or\n   617→\t\t\t// for_each instances are empty, so we return a DynamicVal. We\n   618→\t\t\t// don't really have a good value to return otherwise -- empty\n   619→\t\t\t// values will fail for direct index expressions, and unknown\n   620→\t\t\t// Lists and Maps could fail in some type unifications.\n   621→\t\t\tswitch {\n   622→\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   623→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   624→\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   625→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   626→\t\t\tdefault:\n   627→\t\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(ty), diags\n   628→\t\t\t}\n   629→\n   630→\t\tdefault:\n   631→\t\t\t// We should only end up here during the validate walk,\n   632→\t\t\t// since later walks should have at least partial states populated\n   633→\t\t\t// for all resources in the configuration.\n   634→\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   635→\t\t}\n   636→\t}\n   637→\n   638→\t// Decode all instances in the current state\n   639→\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n   640→\tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\n   641→\tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\n   642→\t\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\n   643→\t\t\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\n   644→\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   645→\t\t\tcontinue\n   646→\t\t}\n   647→\n   648→\t\tinstAddr := addr.Instance(key).Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n   649→\n   650→\t\tchange := d.Evaluator.Changes.GetResourceInstanceChange(instAddr, addrs.NotDeposed)\n   651→\t\tif change != nil {\n   652→\t\t\t// Don't take any resources that are yet to be deleted into account.\n   653→\t\t\t// If the referenced resource is CreateBeforeDestroy, then orphaned\n   654→\t\t\t// instances will be in the state, as they are not destroyed until\n   655→\t\t\t// after their dependants are updated.\n   656→\t\t\tif change.Action == plans.Delete {\n   657→\t\t\t\tif !pendingDestroy {\n   658→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   659→\t\t\t\t}\n   660→\t\t\t}\n   661→\t\t}\n   662→\n   663→\t\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\n   664→\t\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\n   665→\t\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\n   666→\t\t\tif change == nil {\n   667→\t\t\t\t// If the object is in planned status then we should not get\n   668→\t\t\t\t// here, since we should have found a pending value in the plan\n   669→\t\t\t\t// above instead.\n   670→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   671→\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   672→\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Missing pending object in plan\",\n   673→\t\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s is marked as having a change pending but that change is not recorded in the plan. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it.\", instAddr),\n   674→\t\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n   675→\t\t\t\t})\n   676→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   677→\t\t\t}\n   678→\t\t\tval, err := change.After.Decode(ty)\n   679→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   680→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   681→\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   682→\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in plan\",\n   683→\t\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the plan: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n   684→\t\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n   685→\t\t\t\t})\n   686→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   687→\t\t\t}\n   688→\n   689→\t\t\t// If our provider schema contains sensitive values, mark those as sensitive\n   690→\t\t\tafterMarks := change.AfterValMarks\n   691→\t\t\tif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n   692→\t\t\t\tafterMarks = append(afterMarks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n   693→\t\t\t}\n   694→\n   695→\t\t\tinstances[key] = val.MarkWithPaths(afterMarks)\n   696→\t\t\tcontinue\n   697→\t\t}\n   698→\n   699→\t\tios, err := is.Current.Decode(ty)\n   700→\t\tif err != nil {\n   701→\t\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since by the time we get here we\n   702→\t\t\t// should have upgraded the state data already.\n   703→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   704→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   705→\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in state\",\n   706→\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the state: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n   707→\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n   708→\t\t\t})\n   709→\t\t\tcontinue\n   710→\t\t}\n   711→\n   712→\t\tval := ios.Value\n   713→\n   714→\t\t// If our schema contains sensitive values, mark those as sensitive.\n   715→\t\t// Since decoding the instance object can also apply sensitivity marks,\n   716→\t\t// we must remove and combine those before remarking to avoid a double-\n   717→\t\t// mark error.\n   718→\t\tif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n   719→\t\t\tvar marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n   720→\t\t\tval, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n   721→\t\t\tmarks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n   722→\t\t\tval = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n   723→\t\t}\n   724→\t\tinstances[key] = val\n   725→\t}\n   726→\n   727→\t// ret should be populated with a valid value in all cases below\n   728→\tvar ret cty.Value\n   729→\n   730→\tswitch {\n   731→\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   732→\t\t// figure out what the last index we have is\n   733→\t\tlength := -1\n   734→\t\tfor key := range instances {\n   735→\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n   736→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   737→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   738→\t\t\t}\n   739→\t\t\tif int(intKey) >= length {\n   740→\t\t\t\tlength = int(intKey) + 1\n   741→\t\t\t}\n   742→\t\t}\n   743→\n   744→\t\tif length > 0 {\n   745→\t\t\tvals := make([]cty.Value, length)\n   746→\t\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n   747→\t\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n   748→\t\t\t\tif !ok {\n   749→\t\t\t\t\t// old key from state, which isn't valid for evaluation\n   750→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   751→\t\t\t\t}\n   752→\n   753→\t\t\t\tvals[int(intKey)] = instance\n   754→\t\t\t}\n   755→\n   756→\t\t\t// Insert unknown values where there are any missing instances\n   757→\t\t\tfor i, v := range vals {\n   758→\t\t\t\tif v == cty.NilVal {\n   759→\t\t\t\t\tvals[i] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   760→\t\t\t\t}\n   761→\t\t\t}\n   762→\t\t\tret = cty.TupleVal(vals)\n   763→\t\t} else {\n   764→\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyTupleVal\n   765→\t\t}\n   766→\n   767→\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   768→\t\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   769→\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n   770→\t\t\tstrKey, ok := key.(addrs.StringKey)\n   771→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   772→\t\t\t\t// old key that is being dropped and not used for evaluation\n   773→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   774→\t\t\t}\n   775→\t\t\tvals[string(strKey)] = instance\n   776→\t\t}\n   777→\n   778→\t\tif len(vals) > 0 {\n   779→\t\t\t// We use an object rather than a map here because resource schemas\n   780→\t\t\t// may schema.\n   783→\t\t\tret = cty.ObjectVal(vals)\n   784→\t\t} else {\n   785→\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyObjectVal\n   786→\t\t}\n   787→\n   788→\tdefault:\n   789→\t\tval, ok := instances[addrs.NoKey]\n   790→\t\tif !ok {\n   791→\t\t\t// if the instance is missing, insert an unknown value\n   792→\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   793→\t\t}\n   794→\n   795→\t\tret = val\n   796→\t}\n   797→\n   798→\treturn ret, diags\n   799→}\n   800→\n   801→func (d *evaluationStateData) getResourceSchema(addr addrs.Resource, providerAddr addrs.Provider) *configschema.Block {\n   802→\tschema, _, err := 811→\n   812→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetTerraformAttr(addr addrs.TerraformAttr, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   813→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   814→\n The graph walk gradually registers the\n\t// set of instances for each object within the graph nodes for those\n\t// objects, and so as long as the graph has been built correctly the\n\t// set of instances for an object should always be available by the time\n\t// we're evaluating expressions that refer to it.\n\tInstances *instances.Expander\n\n\t// NamedValues is where we keep the values of already-evaluated input\n\t// variables, local values, and output values.\n\tNamedValues *namedvals.State\n\n\t// Plugins is the library of available plugin components (providers and\n\t// provisioners) that we have available to help us evaluate expressions\n\t// that interact with plugin-provided objects.\n\t//\n\t// From this we only access the schemas of the plugins, and don't otherwise\n\t// interact with plugin instances.\n\tPlugins *contextPlugins\n\n\t// State is the current state, embedded in a wrapper that ensures that\n\t// it can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n\tState *states.SyncState\n\n\t// Changes is the set of proposed changes, embedded in a wrapper that\n\t// ensures they can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n\tChanges *plans.ChangesSync\n\n\tPlanTimestamp time.Time\n}\n\n// Scope creates an evaluation scope for the given module path and optional\n// resource.\n//\n// If the \"self\" argument is nil then the \"self\" object is not available\n// in evaluated expressions. diags\n\t}\n\n\t// During the validate walk, input variables are always unknown so\n\t// that we are validating the configuration for all possible input values\n\t// rather than for a specific set. Checking against a specific set of\n\t// input values then happens during the plan walk.\n\t//\n\t// This is important because otherwise the validation walk will tend to be\n\t// overly strict, requiring expressions throughout the configuration to\n\t// be complicated to accommodate all possible inputs, whereas returning\n\t// unknown here allows for simpler patterns like using input values diags\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) GetLocalValue(addr addrs.LocalValue, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\t// First we'll make sure the requested value is declared in configuration,\n\t// so we can produce a nice message if not.\n\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendentForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"local value read from %s, which has no configuration\", d.ModulePath))\n\t}\n\n\tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.Locals[addr.Name]\n\tif config == nil {\n\t\tvar suggestions []string\n\t\tfor k := range moduleConfig.Module.Locals {\n\t\t\tsuggestions = append(suggestions, k)\n\t\t}\n\t\tsuggestion := didyoumean.NameSuggestion(addr.Name, suggestions)\n\t\tif suggestion != \"\" {\n\t\t\tsuggestion = fmt.Sprintf(\" Did you mean %q?\", suggestion)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared local value`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A local value with the name %q has not been declared.%s`, addr.Name, suggestion),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\tval := d.Evaluator.NamedValues.GetLocalValue(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n\treturn val, diags\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) GetModule(addr addrs.ModuleCall, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\t// Output results live in the module that declares them, which is one of\n\t// the child module instances of our current module path.\n\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath.Module().Child(addr.Name)\n\tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n\n\tparentCfg := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendentForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n\tcallConfig, ok := parentCfg.Module.ModuleCalls[addr.Name]\n\tif !ok {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared module`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The configuration contains no %s.`, moduleAddr),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\t// We'll consult the configuration to see what output names we are\n\t// expecting, so we can ensure the resulting object is of the expected\n\t// type even if our data is incomplete for some reason.\n\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.Descendent(moduleAddr)\n\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n\t\t// should never happen, since we have a valid module call above, this\n\t\t// should be caught during static validation.\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"output value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n\t}\n\toutputConfigs := moduleConfig.Module.Outputs\n\n\t// We don't do instance expansion during validation, and so we need to\n\t// return an unknown value. Technically we should always return\n\t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n\t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n\t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n\t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n\t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n\t// validation.\n\t//\n\t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n\t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n\t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n\t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n\tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n\t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n\t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n\t\t}\n\t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n\n\t\tswitch {\n\t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n\t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n\t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n\t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n\t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n\tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n\tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n\tif !known {\n\t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n\t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n\t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n\t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n\t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n\t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n\t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n\t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n\t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n\n\t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n\t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n\t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n\t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n\t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n\t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n\t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n\t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n\t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n\t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n\t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n\t\t}\n\n\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n\t}\n\n\tswitch instKeyType {\n\n\tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n\t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n\t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n\t\t// implementation.\n\t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n\t\t}\n\t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\treturn ret, diags\n\n\tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n\t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n\t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n\t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n\t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n\n\tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n\t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n\n\tdefault:\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n\t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n\t\t\t),\n\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) GetPathAttr(addr addrs.PathAttr, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\tswitch addr.Name {\n\n\tcase \"cwd\":\n\t\tvar err error\n\t\tvar wd string\n\t\tif d.Evaluator.Meta != nil {\n\t\t\t// Meta is always non-nil in the normal case, but some test cases\n\t\t\t// are not so realistic.\n\t\t\twd = d.Evaluator.Meta.OriginalWorkingDir\n\t\t}\n\t\tif wd == \"\" {\n\t\t\twd, err = os.Getwd()\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Failed to get working directory`,\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The value for path.cwd cannot be determined due to a system error: %s`, err),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\t// The current working directory should always be absolute, whether we\n\t\t// just looked it up or whether we were relying on ContextMeta's\n\t\t// (possibly non-normalized) path.\n\t\twd, err = filepath.Abs(wd)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Failed to get working directory`,\n\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The value for path.cwd cannot be determined due to a system error: %s`, err),\n\t\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t}\n\n\t\treturn cty.StringVal(filepath.ToSlash(wd)), diags\n\n\tcase \"module\":\n\t\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendentForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n\t\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n\t\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n\t\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module.path read from module %s, which has no configuration\", d.ModulePath))\n\t\t}\n\t\tsourceDir := moduleConfig.Module.SourceDir\n\t\treturn cty.StringVal(filepath.ToSlash(sourceDir)), diags\n\n\tcase \"root\":\n\t\tsourceDir := d.Evaluator.Config.Module.SourceDir\n\t\treturn cty.StringVal(filepath.ToSlash(sourceDir)), diags\n\n\tdefault:\n\t\tsuggestion := didyoumean.NameSuggestion(addr.Name, []string{\"cwd\", \"module\", \"root\"})\n\t\tif suggestion != \"\" {\n\t\t\tsuggestion = fmt.Sprintf(\" Did you mean %q?\", suggestion)\n\t\t}\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Invalid \"path\" attribute`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The \"path\" object does not have an attribute named %q.%s`, addr.Name, suggestion),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\t// First we'll consult the configuration to see if an resource of this\n\t// name is declared at all.\n\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath\n\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendentForInstance(moduleAddr)\n\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"resource value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n\t}\n\n\tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.ResourceByAddr(addr)\n\tif config == nil {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared resource`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A resource %q %q has not been declared in %s`, addr.Type, addr.Name, moduleDisplayAddr(moduleAddr)),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n\t// state available in all cases.\n\t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n\t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n\tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n\tif schema == nil {\n\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here should've\n\t\t// taken care of it, but we'll show a reasonable error message anyway.\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Missing resource type schema`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"No schema is available for %s in %s. This is a bug in Terraform and should be reported.\", addr, config.Provider),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n\n\trs := d.Evaluator.State.Resource(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n\n\tif rs == nil {\n\t\tswitch d.Operation {\n\t\tcase walkPlan, walkApply:\n\t\t\t// During plan and apply as we evaluate each removed instance they\n\t\t\t// are removed from the working state. Since we know there are no\n\t\t\t// instances, return an empty container of the expected type.\n\t\t\tswitch {\n\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyTupleVal, diags\n\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyObjectVal, diags\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\t// While we can reference an expanded resource with 0\n\t\t\t\t// instances, we cannot reference instances that do not exist.\n\t\t\t\t// Due to the fact that we may have direct references to\n\t\t\t\t// instances that may end up in a root output during destroy\n\t\t\t\t// (since a planned destroy cannot yet remove root outputs), we\n\t\t\t\t// need to return a dynamic value here to allow evaluation to\n\t\t\t\t// continue.\n\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] unknown instance %q referenced during %s\", addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath), d.Operation)\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\tcase walkImport:\n\t\t\t// Import does not yet plan resource changes, so new resources from\n\t\t\t// config are not going to be found here. Once walkImport fully\n\t\t\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\n\t\t\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\n\t\t\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\n\t\t\t// value. This of course will not help if statically known\n\t\t\t// attributes are expected to be known elsewhere, but reduces the\n\t\t\t// number of problematic configs for now.\n\t\t\t// Unlike in plan and apply above we can't be sure the count or\n\t\t\t// for_each instances are empty, so we return a DynamicVal. We\n\t\t\t// don't really have a good value to return otherwise -- empty\n\t\t\t// values will fail for direct index expressions, and unknown\n\t\t\t// Lists and Maps could fail in some type unifications.\n\t\t\tswitch {\n\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(ty), diags\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t// We should only end up here during the validate walk,\n\t\t\t// since later walks should have at least partial states populated\n\t\t\t// for all resources in the configuration.\n\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Decode all instances in the current state\n\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n\tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\n\tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\n\t\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\n\t\t\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\n\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tinstAddr := addr.Instance(key).Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n\n\t\tchange := d.Evaluator.Changes.GetResourceInstanceChange(instAddr, addrs.NotDeposed)\n\t\tif change != nil {\n\t\t\t// Don't take any resources that are yet to be deleted into account.\n\t\t\t// If the referenced resource is CreateBeforeDestroy, then orphaned\n\t\t\t// instances will be in the state, as they are not destroyed until\n\t\t\t// after their dependants are updated.\n\t\t\tif change.Action == plans.Delete {\n\t\t\t\tif !pendingDestroy {\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\n\t\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\n\t\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\n\t\t\tif change == nil {\n\t\t\t\t// If the object is in planned status then we should not get\n\t\t\t\t// here, since we should have found a pending value in the plan\n\t\t\t\t// above instead.\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Missing pending object in plan\",\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s is marked as having a change pending but that change is not recorded in the plan. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it.\", instAddr),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tval, err := change.After.Decode(ty)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in plan\",\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the plan: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// If our provider schema contains sensitive values, mark those as sensitive\n\t\t\tafterMarks := change.AfterValMarks\n\t\t\tif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n\t\t\t\tafterMarks = append(afterMarks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tinstances[key] = val.MarkWithPaths(afterMarks)\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tios, err := is.Current.Decode(ty)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since by the time we get here we\n\t\t\t// should have upgraded the state data already.\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in state\",\n\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the state: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tval := ios.Value\n\n\t\t// If our schema contains sensitive values, mark those as sensitive.\n\t\t// Since decoding the instance object can also apply sensitivity marks,\n\t\t// we must remove and combine those before remarking to avoid a double-\n\t\t// mark error.\n\t\tif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n\t\t\tvar marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n\t\t\tval, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\t\t\tmarks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n\t\t\tval = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n\t\t}\n\t\tinstances[key] = val\n\t}\n\n\t// ret should be populated with a valid value in all cases below\n\tvar ret cty.Value\n\n\tswitch {\n\tcase config.Count != nil:\n\t\t// figure out what the last index we have is\n\t\tlength := -1\n\t\tfor key := range instances {\n\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif int(intKey) >= length {\n\t\t\t\tlength = int(intKey) + 1\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif length > 0 {\n\t\t\tvals := make([]cty.Value, length)\n\t\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n\t\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n\t\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\t\t// old key from state, which isn't valid for evaluation\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\tvals[int(intKey)] = instance\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Insert unknown values where there are any missing instances\n\t\t\tfor i, v := range vals {\n\t\t\t\tif v == cty.NilVal {\n\t\t\t\t\tvals[i] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tret = cty.TupleVal(vals)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyTupleVal\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n\t\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n\t\t\tstrKey, ok := key.(addrs.StringKey)\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\t// old key that is being dropped and not used for evaluation\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tvals[string(strKey)] = instance\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif len(vals) > 0 {\n\t\t\t// We use an object rather than a map here because resource schemas\n\t\t\t// may include dynamically-typed attributes, which will then cause\n\t\t\t// each instance to potentially have a different runtime type even\n\t\t\t// though they all conform to the static schema.\n\t\t\tret = cty.ObjectVal(vals)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyObjectVal\n\t\t}\n\n\tdefault:\n\t\tval, ok := instances[addrs.NoKey]\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t// if the instance is missing, insert an unknown value\n\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tret = val\n\t}\n\n\treturn ret, diags\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) getResourceSchema(addr addrs.Resource, providerAddr addrs.Provider) *configschema.Block {\n\tschema, _, err := d.Evaluator.Plugins.ResourceTypeSchema(providerAddr, addr.Mode, addr.Type)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\t// We have plently other codepaths that will detect and report\n\t\t// schema lookup errors before we'd reach this point, so we'll just\n\t\t// treat a failure here the same as having no schema.\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\treturn schema\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) GetTerraformAttr(addr addrs.TerraformAttr, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tif d.Evaluator.Meta == nil || d.Evaluator.Meta.Env == \"\" {\n\t\t// The absense of an \"env\" (really: workspace) name suggests that\n\t\t// we're running in a non-workspace context, such as in a component\n\t\t// of a stack. terraform.workspace -- and the terraform symbol in\n\t\t// general -- is a legacy thing from workspaces mode that isn't\n\t\t// carried forward to stacks, because stack configurations can instead\n\t\t// vary their behavior based on input variables provided in the\n\t\t// deployment {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01BxAYLcyMXU4ZzjS5bditTk","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→// Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\n     2→// SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\n     3→\n     4→package objchange\n     5→\n     6→import (\n     7→\t\"errors\"\n     8→\t\"fmt\"\n     9→\n    10→\t\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\"\n    11→\n    12→\t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/configs/configschema\"\n    13→)\n    14→\n    15→// ProposedNew constructs a proposed new object value by combining the\n    16→// computed attribute values from \"prior\" with the configured attribute values\n    17→// from \"config\".\n    18→//\n    19→// Both value must conform to the given schema's implied type, or this function\n    20→// will panic.\n    21→//\n    22→// The prior value must be wholly known, but the config value may be unknown\n    23→// or have nested unknown values.\n    24→//\n    25→// The merging of the two objects includes the attributes of any nested blocks,\n    26→// which will be correlated in a manner appropriate for their nesting mode.\n    27→// Note in particular that the correlation for blocks backed by sets is a\n    28→// heuristic based on matching non-computed attribute values and so it may\n    29→// produce strange results with more \"extreme\" cases, such as a nested set\n    30→// block where _all_ attributes are computed.\n    31→func ProposedNew(schema *configschema.Block, prior, config cty.Value) cty.Value {\n    32→\t// If the config and prior are both null, return early here before\n    33→\t// populating the prior block. The prevents non-null blocks from appearing\n    34→\t// the proposed state value.\n    35→\tif config.IsNull() && prior.IsNull() {\n    36→\t\treturn prior\n    37→\t}\n    38→\n    39→\tif prior.IsNull() {\n    40→\t\t// In this case, we will construct a synthetic prior value that is\n    41→\t\t// similar to the result of decoding an empty configuration block,\n    42→\t\t// which simplifies our handling of the top-level attributes/blocks\n    43→\t\t// below by giving us one non-null level of object to pull values from.\n    44→\t\t//\n    45→\t\t// \"All attributes null\" happens to be the definition of EmptyValue for\n    46→\t\t// a Block, so we can just delegate to that\n    47→\t\tprior = schema.EmptyValue()\n    48→\t}\n    49→\treturn proposedNew(schema, prior, config)\n    50→}\n    51→\n    52→// PlannedDataResourceObject is similar to proposedNewBlock but tailored for\n    53→// planning data resources in particular. Specifically, it replaces the values\n    54→// of any Computed attributes not set in the configuration with an unknown\n    55→// value, which serves as a placeholder for a value to be filled in by the\n    56→// provider when the data resource is finally read.\n    57→//\n    58→// Data resources are different because the planning of them is handled\n    59→// entirely within Terraform Core and not subject to customization by the\n    60→// provider. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_018tAHRPFU3vhCfzrfYC73Gx","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01LAesUmJ2MHcjYxBoWcuKaD","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nPhantom in-place updates occur because Terraform's state serialization layer only records sensitivity marks from variable references, not from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations. When resources are refreshed and planned, the absence of schema-defined sensitive marks causes an asymmetry in mark comparisons, triggering spurious Update actions even when values haven't changed.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause spans multiple layers:\n\n1. **State serialization gap**: Provider responses don't include sensitivity marks (providers don't mark values). When encoding state, the code extracts marks from the value and stores them in `AttrSensitivePaths`, but only variable-based marks exist on the value at save time—schema marks were never applied.\n\n2. **Mark restoration incomplete**: When state is decoded and during refresh, only the stored marks from `AttrSensitivePaths` are re-applied. Schema marks are never restored at the state layer.\n\n3. **Asymmetric mark comparison in plan**: During planning, a second check (line 1208 of `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`) compares marks between prior and planned values even when values are identical. If marks differ, the action is upgraded from `NoOp` to `Update`.\n\n4. **Evaluator compensation creates asymmetry**: The evaluator's `GetResource()` method applies schema marks when values are read for expression evaluation, but this happens in the expression evaluation path, not when currentState is passed to the plan function. This creates an asymmetry where:\n   - `priorPaths` (from state): contains only variable marks\n   - `unmarkedPaths` (from config): contains marks from the configuration\n   - These can differ due to different variable references or schema mark application\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File: `internal/states/instance_object.go` (lines 94-137)\n\nThe `Encode()` method extracts marks at save time:\n```go\n// Line 98-99: Extract marks from value\nval, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Line 131: Save only the marks that existed on the value\nAttrSensitivePaths: pvm,\n```\n\n**Problem**: If a provider returns an unmarked value for a schema-sensitive attribute, no mark is extracted. Schema marks are only on values when applied by the evaluator downstream.\n\n### File: `internal/states/instance_object_src.go` (lines 77-104)\n\nThe `Decode()` method restores only stored marks:\n```go\n// Lines 89-90: Re-apply stored marks from state file\nif os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**: No schema marks are restored because they were never recorded in the state file.\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go` (lines 580-723)\n\nThe `refresh()` method handles prior marks:\n```go\n// Lines 623-626: Extract marks from prior state value\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n\n// Lines 718-720: Re-apply only variable marks to refreshed value\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**: Only variable marks (from state) are re-applied. Schema marks are never added.\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go` (lines 1199-1210)\n\nThe `plan()` method triggers phantom Updates:\n```go\n// Lines 1082-1083: Unmarked values are equal (no actual change)\neqV := unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)\neq := eqV.IsKnown() && eqV.True()\n\n// Line 1090-1091: Action is set to NoOp\ncase eq && !matchedForceReplace:\n    action = plans.NoOp\n\n// Lines 1199-1210: But then marks are compared\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**: Even though values are identical, different mark sets (variable vs. schema) trigger an Update action.\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/evaluate.go` (lines 689-693, 714-723)\n\nThe evaluator applies schema marks when reading resources:\n```go\n// Lines 689-693: For planned objects\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    afterMarks = append(afterMarks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n}\n\n// Lines 714-723: For current state objects\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\n**Key finding**: Schema marks are only applied by the evaluator when resources are read for expression evaluation. They are NOT applied when:\n- State is decoded from disk\n- Refresh returns values to the plan node\n- The plan node compares prior vs. planned values\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/marks.go` (lines 17-58)\n\nMark comparison and filtering functions:\n```go\n// Lines 17-26: Filter marks that don't apply to a value\nfunc filterMarks(val cty.Value, marks []cty.PathValueMarks) []cty.PathValueMarks {\n    var res []cty.PathValueMarks\n    for _, mark := range marks {\n        if _, err := mark.Path.Apply(val); err == nil {\n            res = append(res, mark)\n        }\n    }\n    return res\n}\n\n// Lines 31-58: Compare mark sets for equality\nfunc marksEqual(a, b []cty.PathValueMarks) bool {\n    // ... checks if two mark sets are identical ...\n}\n```\n\nThese are called from line 1208 to detect mark differences.\n\n### File: `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go` (lines 402-411)\n\nJSON output generation applies schema marks at presentation layer:\n```go\n// Lines 402-406: JSON output applies schema marks on-demand\nvalue, marks := riObj.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(value, nil)...)\n}\ns := SensitiveAsBool(value.MarkWithPaths(marks))\n```\n\n**Key finding**: The JSON output \"compensates\" by applying schema marks when generating output, but these marks don't exist in the state file itself. This is why `terraform show -json` shows complete `sensitive_values` even though the state file doesn't have schema marks recorded.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/states/`**: State serialization (encode/decode) only stores variable-based marks\n2. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`**: Refresh and plan functions don't apply schema marks; phantom diff detection (lines 1199-1210)\n3. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`**: Only the expression evaluator applies schema marks, creating asymmetry\n4. **`internal/terraform/marks.go`**: Mark comparison triggers Update actions on mark differences\n5. **`internal/command/jsonstate/`**: Compensates at presentation layer but doesn't fix root cause\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider response**: Provider returns resource value WITHOUT any sensitivity marks (correct behavior—providers don't mark values)\n\n2. **State encoding**: The value's marks are extracted and stored in `AttrSensitivePaths`. If the value has marks from sensitive variables, those are stored. But schema-defined marks are NOT on the value, so they are NOT stored.\n\n3. **State file persistence**: `sensitive_attributes` in the state file contains only variable-based marks. Schema marks are completely absent.\n\n4. **State decoding**: When state is read, the stored marks (variable marks only) are re-applied via `Decode()`. Schema marks are not re-applied because they don't exist in the stored state.\n\n5. **Refresh execution**: The prior value (with variable marks) is sent to the provider. The response (unmarked) is received. Prior marks are extracted and re-applied to the refreshed value. The refreshed state has variable marks but NOT schema marks.\n\n6. **Plan execution**: The currentState (from refresh) is passed with variable marks only. Configuration is evaluated. Provider is called. Response is unmarked and re-applied with config marks.\n\n7. **Mark comparison**: Line 1208 compares marks between prior (variable marks) and planned (config marks). These can differ even though values are identical.\n\n8. **Phantom Update**: If marks are different, the action is upgraded from `NoOp` to `Update`, creating a phantom in-place change.\n\n9. **JSON output manifestation**: When `terraform show -json` is run, the jsonstate layer applies schema marks on-demand, creating complete `sensitive_values`. But the state file itself never had these schema marks, so they are lost across Terraform runs.\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires recording schema-defined sensitive marks in the state file itself. Three approaches are possible:\n\n1. **Record schema marks at encode time** (cleanest): Modify `instance_object.go::Encode()` to:\n   - Accept the resource schema as a parameter\n   - Apply schema marks to the value before extraction\n   - Store both variable and schema marks in `AttrSensitivePaths`\n   - This requires threading the schema through the encode pipeline\n\n2. **Apply schema marks at decode time** (moderate): Modify `instance_object_src.go::Decode()` to:\n   - Accept the resource schema as a parameter\n   - Apply schema marks after restoring stored marks\n   - Risk: breaks the current contract that Decode() knows nothing about schema\n\n3. **Fix the asymmetry in plan comparison** (band-aid): Modify `node_resource_abstract_instance.go::plan()` to:\n   - Apply schema marks to currentState.Value before comparison\n   - Requires accessing schema in the plan function\n   - Doesn't fix root cause: schema marks still absent from state file\n\n**Diagnostic steps**:\n1. This creates an asymmetry:\n\n1. **State encoding gap** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`): When saving state, only marks on the value are stored. Since providers don't return marked values, schema-defined sensitive attributes never get their marks recorded.\n\n2. **Incomplete state restoration** (`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`): When state is decoded, only the stored marks are re-applied—schema marks don't exist to be restored.\n\n3. **Refresh asymmetry** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:580-723`): The refresh function re-applies variable marks but not schema marks.\n\n4. **Phantom diff detection** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1199-1210`): During planning, even identical values trigger an Update action if their mark sets differ, because:\n   - `priorPaths` contains only variable marks (from state)\n   - `unmarkedPaths` contains config evaluation marks\n   - These differ → action is upgraded from NoOp to Update\n\n5. **Evaluator compensation** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go:689-723`): The evaluator applies schema marks when reading resources for expression evaluation, but NOT when state is decoded at the state layer or when values are compared in the plan node. This creates the asymmetry.\n\n6. **JSON output manifestation** (`internal/command/jsonstate/state.go:402-411`): The JSON generation layer applies schema marks on-demand, which is why `terraform show -json` appears correct even though the state file is incomplete.\n\nThe investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with complete evidence, affected components, causal chain, and diagnostic steps.","stop_reason":null,"session_id":"6f97bf89-4f4f-41ce-8c00-a4e592d10acf","total_cost_usd":0.35943129999999995,"usage":{"input_tokens":381,"cache_creation_input_tokens":68562,"cache_read_input_tokens":1959878,"output_tokens":15472,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":68562,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"},"modelUsage":{"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001":{"inputTokens":381,"outputTokens":15472,"cacheReadInputTokens":1959878,"cacheCreationInputTokens":68562,"webSearchRequests":0,"costUSD":0.35943129999999995,"contextWindow":200000,"maxOutputTokens":32000}},"permission_denials":[],"fast_mode_state":"off","uuid":"805a97d7-5122-4db4-a4cc-5f307ea3b83c"}
